GEOTECHNICAL ENGINEERING CONSTRUCTION OBSERVATION 
ANCHOR INSTALLATION AND TESTING 
EMERGENCY REPAIRS IN THE VICINITY OF 4120 ROUNDTOP DRIVE, PHASE 1 
JOB NO. 32-21 
HONOLULU, OAHU, HAWAII 
Dear Mr. Ding: 
This letter report summarizes our geotechnical observation services performed 
during the installation and testing of the pre-production sacrificial and production anchors 
for the Round Top Drive Phase 1 project located in the Honolulu area on the Island of 
Oahu, Hawaii.  The project location and general vicinity are shown on the Project Location 
Map, Plate 1. 
In general, this letter report presents our observations and the results of the 
grouted anchor installation and testing performed on the selected anchors for the project 
from May 24 through October 31, 2022. Prometheus Construction was the general 
contractor responsible for the installation and testing of the anchors. 
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS 
The Round Top Drive Phase 1 project is located along the downslope side of the 
roadway fronting 4120 Round Top Drive in the Tantalus area of Honolulu on the island of 
Oahu, Hawaii. Due to a heavy rainstorm on December 6, 2021, inducing saturated slope 
ground conditions, a catastrophic road collapse occurred fronting 4120 Round Top Drive. 
This project involved excavation and installation of three tiers of soil nail retaining walls 
to mitigate and restore the collapsed slope and roadway. 
AECOM 
Page 2 
W.O. 8386-10 
September 29, 2023 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
Geolabs, Inc. provided geotechnical engineering consultation services in support 
of the project design and construction management. The geotechnical engineering 
services during construction consisted of observing soil nail anchor installation and testing 
for general conformance with the project plans, specifications and geotechnical design 
recommendations. 
SOIL NAIL INSTALLATION AND TESTING 
To restore the collapsed steep earth slope and roadway above, three-tier soil nail 
retaining walls were designed and constructed, consisting of nine rows of soil nail anchors 
with a total of 131 individual reinforcing bars grouted in the drilled boreholes stabilizing 
the existing slope. Three layers of shotcrete facings were installed on each tier of the 
retaining wall with structural reinforcing placed prior to the initial and final shotcrete layers, 
including a 2-inch flash coating, 4-inch initial shotcrete facing, and a final 9-inch shotcrete 
facing. 
Due to revisions of the return walls on each side of the third bench, the distance 
between the deflection points was reduced by approximately 7 feet to accommodate the 
existing slope geometry, resulting in the removal of one column (3 soil nails) from the middle 
portion of the third bench face. 
The grouted soil nail installations and proof tests were performed by Prometheus 
Construction. The approximate locations of the grouted rock anchors are shown on the 
Anchor Location Plan, Plate 2. Installation and testing of the anchors were conducted from 
June 18 to October 30, 2022, with shotcrete placement. A summary of the soil nail 
installations and testing are presented on Plates 3.1 through 3.4. Details of the soil nail 
installation records are provided in Appendix A, Plates A-1.1 through A-3.74. 
Soil Nail Installation 
A Geolabs representative observed the drilling and grouting operations during the 
construction of the soil nails. The soil nails on the upper tier were drilled using a TEI HT 360 
rock drill mounted a CAT 315C with a 5-inch drill bit. The soil nails on the middle and lower 
tiers were drilled using a Menzi Muck A61 spider excavator mounted with a TEI HT 260 rock 
drill and 5-inch drill bit. 
The soil nails were drilled to a depth of approximately 25 feet from the slope face with 
an approximate inclination of about 20 degrees from horizontal, except for soil nails on the 
south return wall of the middle tier that were drilled to a depth of 20 feet to avoid interfering 
with the existing structure foundation.   
Considering loose consistency of the in-situ volcanic cinder soil conditions, the soil 
nails were drilled using a B7X Geo-Drill bar with a diameter of 1.5-inch. The hollow core bar 
allows for the injection of a cement-based slurry while drilling to prevent a cave-in and 
penetrating cementitious into the loose soil conditions for improvements. After the hole was 
drilled to the specified tip, a production grout with a design 28-day compressive strength of 
4,000 psi was pumped from bottom to top until fresh grout appeared at the top of the 
AECOM 
Page 3 
W.O. 8386-10 
September 29, 2023 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
borehole. The grout cover around the hollow core bar was maintained by utilizing the 
centralizers. 
Soil Nail Testing 
Prior to the production of soil nail construction, two sacrificial testing soil nails, 
designated as T-1 and T-2, were installed to verify the adequacy of the soil nail pull-out 
resistance. The first Test Nail T-1 was installed on March 3, 2022, extending to a depth of 
20 feet, and verification tested on March 11, 2022. Due to inadequate bonded length, the 
Test Nail T-1 was not able to achieve the required capacity meeting the design load capacity 
of 35 kips with a factor of safety of 1.5. 
Subsequently, the second Test Nail T-2 was installed on March 14, 2022, extending 
to a depth of 25 feet, and verification tested on March 21, 2022. The testing apparatus 
included a 75-ton hydraulic jack (Orbit 75/6 – S/N 72019) and a 1-inch stroke dial gauge. 
The test was conducted by pre-loading the testing apparatus up to about 10 kips to engage 
the reaction timbers and ground. The verification soil nail was then loaded up to about 150 
percent of the design load (35 kips). The soil nail was tested to the maximum test load of 
about 52.5 kips with a total displacement of about 0.862 inches. 
Based on the results of the pull-out testing of the Test Nail T-2, the production soil 
nail load capacity was reduced to 30 kips with a length of 25 feet to accommodate the poor 
in-situ loose soil conditions. Detailed test soil nail installation recorded are presented on 
Plates 4.1 through 4.4. Results of the verification tests, including Load versus Displacement 
and the Creep Movement versus Time curves, are presented on Plates 5.1 through 5.7. 
In addition, three production soil nails, designated as C-6, F-12 and I-7, were selected 
for proof testing to verify the soil nail pull-out resistance. The proof testing was conducted 
between June 13 and October 31, 2022 to the maximum testing load of about 133 percent 
of the revised design load capacity of 30 kips. Total displacement measured for Soil Nail 
Nos. C-6, F-12, and I-7 were 0.260, 0.163, and 0.214, respectively. Subsequently, the proof 
testing soil nail anchors were continuously loaded up to 150 percent of the design capacity 
with total displacement of less than 0.3 inches. Results of the proof tests, including Load 
versus Displacement and the Creep Movement versus Time curves, are presented on 
Plates 6.1 through 6.9. 
Based on the observations of our field representatives, we believe that the 
specified soil nails observed by Geolabs have been installed in general conformance with 
the project plans and specifications and within the limits of generally accepted 
construction practices. Based on our observations of the soil nail tests performed by the 
contractor, it is our professional opinion that the soil nails have been installed to provide 
the sufficient load capacity with tolerable movements. 
AECOM Page 4
W.O. 8386-10
September 29, 2023
LIMITATIONS
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities
occurring simultaneously on a construction site; therefore, some of the work for the
grouted anchor installation and testing may have occurred without our direct observation.
However, we believe that the level of geotechnical observation provided is reasonable in
reducing the geotechnical risks to the project.
Our services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards of
geotechnical engineering practice; no warranty is expressed or implied. Provision of
construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance, nor does it guarantee construction
of any type. The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of their work, for adhering
to the plans and specifications, and for repairing defects regardless of when they are found.
CLOSURE
We appreciate the opportunity to provide geotechnical engineering services to
AECOM on this project. If you have questions or need additional information, please contact
our Office.
Respectfully submitted,
